# Context Mode Index

Index local project content for later search.

## Instructions

1. Prefer the `ctx_index` MCP tool when it is available.
2. Ask for a path only if the user did not provide one and the current project root is ambiguous.
3. Use `path`, not large inline `content`, so file bytes do not enter the conversation.
4. For repository indexing, pass conservative bounds and a clear source label:

```javascript
ctx_index({
  path: ".",
  source: "project:<name>",
  maxDepth: 5,
  maxFiles: 200
})
```

5. If MCP tools are unavailable, fall back to the CLI:

```bash
context-mode index . --source project:<name>
```

6. Report the indexed source label, file count or section count, and the matching search command:

```javascript
ctx_search({ source: "project:<name>", queries: ["..."] })
```

## Safety

- Do not index dependency directories, build outputs, secrets, or generated artifacts.
- Prefer `--exclude` or `exclude` for project-specific noisy paths.
- For broad repos, ask the user before raising `maxFiles` above 500.

# Context Mode Index

Index local project content for later search.

## Instructions

1. Prefer the `ctx_index` MCP tool when it is available.
2. Ask for a path only if the user did not provide one and the current project root is ambiguous.
3. Use `path`, not large inline `content`, so file bytes do not enter the conversation.
4. For repository indexing, pass conservative bounds and a clear source label:

```javascript
ctx_index({
  path: ".",
  source: "project:<name>",
  maxDepth: 5,
  maxFiles: 200
})
```

5. If MCP tools are unavailable, fall back to the CLI:

```bash
context-mode index . --source project:<name>
```

6. Report the indexed source label, file count or section count, and the matching search command:

```javascript
ctx_search({ source: "project:<name>", queries: ["..."] })
```

## Safety

- Do not index dependency directories, build outputs, secrets, or generated artifacts.
- Prefer `--exclude` or `exclude` for project-specific noisy paths.
- For broad repos, ask the user before raising `maxFiles` above 500.

1	#!/usr/bin/env python
2	#
3	# get_proxied_fqdns
4	#
5	# Outputs a JSON dictionary of all FQDNs that are proxied through Cloudflare together with their backends.  This
6	# information is used by the ITS Web Hosting inventory script to map website FQDNs to server or pool names, but it can
7	# also be used for other purposes.
8	#
9	# If run using an API token, the token should have only the
10	# permission DNS:Read but for all zones.  The script can also be
11	# run using credentials from the CLOUDFLARE_EMAIL and
12	# CLOUDFLARE_API_KEY environment variables.
13	#
14	
15	import argparse
16	import json
17	import logging
18	import os
19	import sys
20	
21	import rich.logging
22	import rich.progress
23	from rich.console import Console
24	from rich.pretty import pprint
25	
26	
27	CLOUDFLARE_ACCOUNT_ID = 'b6a4063d6fa89fba31cf8bf99540d7e5'  # Regents of the University of Michigan
28	
29	parser = argparse.ArgumentParser(description='Get JSON dictionary of all FQDNs proxied through our Cloudflare account.')
30	parser.add_argument(
31	    '--output', '-o',
32	    type=argparse.FileType('w'),
33	    default=sys.stdout,
34	    help='output file name; defaults to stdout'
35	)
36	parser.add_argument(
37	    '--no-certcheck',
38	    action='store_true',
39	    default=False,
40	    help='skip FQDNs that have the no-certcheck tag in Cloudflare'
41	)
42	parser.add_argument(
43	    '--verbose', '-v',
44	    action='count',
45	    default=0,
46	    help='increase the level of detail in the output; can be specified multiple times'
47	)
48	options = parser.parse_args()
49	
50	console = Console()
51	console_style = {
52	    'status': '[bold green]',
53	    'error': '[bold red]',
54	}
55	
56	if options.verbose >= 2:
57	    os.environ['CLOUDFLARE_LOG'] = 'info'
58	    logging.basicConfig(
59	        level=logging.INFO, format="%(message)s", datefmt="[%X]",
60	        handlers=[rich.logging.RichHandler(console=console, markup=True, rich_tracebacks=True)]
61	    )
62	import cloudflare
63	
64	
65	def verbose_log(*args, **kwargs) -> None:
66	    verbosity = 1
67	    if 'verbosity' in kwargs:
68	        verbosity = kwargs['verbosity']
69	        del kwargs['verbosity']
70	    if options.verbose >= verbosity:
71	        console.log(*args, _stack_offset=2, **kwargs)
72	
73	
74	class CFProgress:
75	    """
76	    Wrap a Cloudflare object to provide Rich progress updates.
77	    """
78	    def __init__(self, obj, progress, task):
79	        self.cf_obj = obj
80	        self.progress = progress
81	        self.task = task
82	        self.cf_iter = None
83	        if hasattr(self.cf_obj, 'result_info'):
84	            self.progress.update(self.task, total=obj.result_info.total_count, refresh=True)
85	
86	    def __iter__(self):
87	        if self.cf_iter is None:
88	            self.cf_iter = self.cf_obj.__iter__()
89	        return self
90	
91	    def __next__(self):
92	        n = self.cf_iter.__next__()
93	        self.progress.advance(self.task, advance=1)
94	        return n
95	
96	
97	def progress_bar() -> rich.progress.Progress:
98	    return rich.progress.Progress(
99	        rich.progress.TextColumn("[progress.description]{task.description}"),
100	        rich.progress.MofNCompleteColumn(),
101	        rich.progress.BarColumn(),
102	        rich.progress.TaskProgressColumn(),
103	        rich.progress.TimeElapsedColumn(),
104	        rich.progress.TimeRemainingColumn(),
105	        console=console,
106	        transient=False if options.verbose else True,
107	    )
108	
109	
110	def main() -> None:
111	
112	    verbose_log('Getting list of zones...')
113	    cf = cloudflare.Cloudflare()
114	    with progress_bar() as progress:
115	        task = progress.add_task('Getting list of zones', total=None)
116	        zones = list(CFProgress(cf.zones.list(account={'id': CLOUDFLARE_ACCOUNT_ID}), progress, task))
117	    zone_count = len(zones)
118	    verbose_log(f'Found {zone_count} zones')
119	
120	    websites = {}
121	    blank = ' '
122	    with progress_bar() as progress:
123	        zone_name = blank
124	        zone_task = progress.add_task(f'Checking zone:  {zone_name:32s}', total=zone_count)
125	        for zone in zones:
126	            progress.update(zone_task, description=f'Checking zone:  {zone.name:32s}', advance=1)
127	            dns_records = cf.dns.records.list(zone_id=zone.id, proxied=True)
128	            for dns_record in dns_records:
129	                if options.no_certcheck and 'no-certcheck' in dns_record.tags:
130	                    verbose_log(f'  skipping {dns_record.name} because of no-certcheck tag')
131	                    continue
132	                r_name = dns_record.name
133	                r_value = dns_record.content
134	                if r_name not in websites:
135	                    websites[r_name] = [r_value]
136	                else:
137	                    websites[r_name].append(r_value)
138	
139	    verbose_log(f'Total websites: {len(websites)}')
140	    print(json.dumps(websites, indent=4, sort_keys=True), file=options.output)
141	
142	
143	if __name__ == '__main__':
144	    main()
145
```

2	import sys

5	from cloudflare import Cloudflare
6	from rich.pretty import pprint
7	
8	import script_context as sc
9	
10	
11	def get_cloudflare_ips():
12	
13	    global cloudflare_ipv4_nets, cloudflare_ipv6_nets
14	
15	    cf = sc.config['Cloudflare']
16	    api_token = cf.get('api_token')
17	    if api_token:
18	        cloudflare = Cloudflare(api_token=api_token)
19	    else:
20	        email = cf.get('email')
21	        api_key = cf.get('api_key')
22	        if not email or not api_key:
23	            sys.exit('ERROR: [Cloudflare] is enabled but needs either api_token, '
24	                     'or both email and api_key.')
25	        cloudflare = Cloudflare(api_email=email, api_key=api_key)
26	
27	    with sc.console.status('[bold green]Getting Cloudflare IP ranges ...'):
28	        try:
29	            cloudflare_ips = cloudflare.ips.list()
30	        except Exception as e:
31	            sys.exit(f'ERROR: Unable to get lists of Cloudflare IPs: {e}')
32	        if sc.options.verbose > 2:
33	            sc.debug('Cloudfare IPs:')
34	            pprint(cloudflare_ips)
35	        sc.plugin_context['plugin.cloudflare']['cloudflare_ipv4_nets'] = [ipaddress.ip_network(cidr) for cidr in cloudflare_ips.ipv4_cidrs]
36	        sc.plugin_context['plugin.cloudflare']['cloudflare_ipv6_nets'] = [ipaddress.ip_network(cidr) for cidr in cloudflare_ips.ipv6_cidrs]
37	
38	
39	def get_cloudflare_ipv4_nets():
40	    return cloudflare_ipv4_nets
41	
42	
43	def get_cloudflare_ipv6_nets():
44	    return cloudflare_ipv6_nets

## Summary of the critical finding

`fqdns.json` is loaded into a local variable `proxied_fqdns` and is consumed in **exactly one place**, using **only the `in` membership operator against the dict's keys**. The values (the arrays of DNS origins) are **never read, indexed, or iterated**. It is never stored in `sc.*`, `site_context`, or any global — it is a plain local variable inside the per-site loop.

## 1. Every place `fqdns.json` / its path variable is referenced

All references live in one contiguous block. Filename literal and the path variable `proxied_fqdns_file`:

- Line 1565 (comment): `#   get_proxied_fqdns --output fqdns.json`
- Line 1567: `proxied_fqdns_file = "fqdns.json"`
- Lines 1568–1569: symlink resolution
- Line 1570: staleness check (mtime &gt; 86400s = 1 day)
- Line 1576: `"Exiting because --all was specified. Please update fqdns.json"`
- Line 1578–1579: the actual read

Verbatim (lines 1563–1579):

```python
        # Get the list of all proxied Cloudflare FQDNs.
        # This file is created by running the following cloudflare-support-tools command:
        #   get_proxied_fqdns --output fqdns.json
        # Warn if the file pointed to by the symlink is more than a day old.
        proxied_fqdns_file = "fqdns.json"
        if os.path.islink(proxied_fqdns_file):
            proxied_fqdns_file = os.readlink(proxied_fqdns_file)
        if time.time() - os.path.getmtime(proxied_fqdns_file) &gt; 86400:
            sc.console.print(
                f":exclamation: [bold red] ATTENTION: {proxied_fqdns_file} is more than a day old!"
            )
            if sc.options.all:
                sys.exit(
                    "Exiting because --all was specified. Please update fqdns.json"
                )
        with open(proxied_fqdns_file, "r") as f:
            proxied_fqdns = json.load(f)
```

Note: `fqdns.json` is expected to be a **symlink** to the real dated file (lines 1568–1569 resolve it before the mtime check).

## 2. &amp; 5. The data structure the code depends on

The loaded object is used **only** at line 1652:

```python
                    if dns_points_at_cloudflare &gt; 0:
                        if hostname not in proxied_fqdns:
                            sc.console.print(
                                f":exclamation: [bold red] ATTENTION: {hostname} is behind Cloudflare but not proxied"
                            )
                            behind_cloudflare_not_proxied.append(hostname)
                        else:
                            fqdns_behind_cloudflare.append(hostname)
```

`hostname not in proxied_fqdns` — since `proxied_fqdns` is a dict (JSON object), `in` tests membership against the **keys** (the FQDN strings). That is the entire dependency.

There is **no** `proxied_fqdns[...]` indexing, **no** `[0]`, **no** `.get()`, **no** iteration over its values, and **no** iteration over the dict at all. Confirmed by the complete grep of every `proxied_fqdns` occurrence:

```
1565:        #   get_proxied_fqdns --output fqdns.json
1567:        proxied_fqdns_file = "fqdns.json"
1568:        if os.path.islink(proxied_fqdns_file):
1569:            proxied_fqdns_file = os.readlink(proxied_fqdns_file)
1570:        if time.time() - os.path.getmtime(proxied_fqdns_file) &gt; 86400:
1572:                f":exclamation: [bold red] ATTENTION: {proxied_fqdns_file} is more than a day old!"
1578:        with open(proxied_fqdns_file, "r") as f:
1579:            proxied_fqdns = json.load(f)
1652:                        if hostname not in proxied_fqdns:
```

**Answer to "what breaks if I change values from `array` to `{zone_id, origins}`": nothing breaks.** The code only relies on the top-level FQDN strings being the dict keys. Since `in` on a dict ignores values entirely, changing each value from `[...]` (array of origins) to `{"zone_id": ..., "origins": [...]}` is completely transparent to this program. The only structural requirement is that `json.load` returns something supporting `in` by FQDN string — i.e., the top level must stay an object/dict keyed by FQDN (or any container where `hostname in x` is a valid membership test). If you changed the top level from an object to, say, a list of objects, then `hostname not in proxied_fqdns` would silently change meaning and break.

## 3. Where the loaded data is stored and consumed downstream

- **Storage:** Purely a local variable `proxied_fqdns` (line 1579), inside the main per-site loop. It is NOT assigned to `sc.`, NOT to `site_context`, NOT to `sc.plugin_context`, NOT to any global. (The Cloudflare IP network ranges used by the DNS classifier come from a *different* source — `sc.plugin_context["plugin.cloudflare"]["cloudflare_ipv4_nets"]` / `..._ipv6_nets`, lines 1623 &amp; 1626 — not from `fqdns.json`.)

- **Consumption:** The single site at line 1652, which populates two local lists:
  - `behind_cloudflare_not_proxied` (line 1656) — hostname resolves to a Cloudflare IP but its FQDN is NOT a key in `proxied_fqdns`.
  - `fqdns_behind_cloudflare` (line 1658) — hostname resolves to Cloudflare AND is a key in `proxied_fqdns` (i.e., proxying is on).

These downstream lists (`fqdns_behind_cloudflare`, `fqdns_not_behind_cloudflare`, `behind_cloudflare_not_proxied`, `not_in_dns`) drive the email/notice generation later (e.g. lines 1773, 1930, 2175, 2275), but those consumers use the derived lists, not `proxied_fqdns` itself.

## 4. `classify_hostname_dns` and whether fqdns data feeds it

`classify_hostname_dns` is defined at lines 1067–1134 and called at lines 1619–1629. **`proxied_fqdns` does NOT feed into it.** Its signature (lines 1067–1073):

```python
def classify_hostname_dns(
    hostname: str,
    site_name: str,
    cloudflare_enabled: bool,
    cf_v4_nets: list,
    cf_v6_nets: list,
) -&gt; (int, int, list, bool):
```

It resolves the hostname's A/AAAA records and counts how many addresses fall inside the Cloudflare IP ranges (`cf_v4_nets`/`cf_v6_nets`), returning `(points_at_cloudflare, points_elsewhere, notices, transient)`. The membership check against `proxied_fqdns` happens *after* this call, back in the caller at line 1652, using the returned `dns_points_at_cloudflare` count to decide whether to consult `proxied_fqdns`.

The call site (lines 1614–1629) passes the Cloudflare net ranges from plugin context, not from `fqdns.json`:

```python
                (
                    dns_points_at_cloudflare,
                    dns_points_elsewhere,
                    dns_notices,
                    dns_transient,
                ) = classify_hostname_dns(
                    hostname,
                    site["name"],
                    cloudflare_enabled,
                    sc.plugin_context["plugin.cloudflare"]["cloudflare_ipv4_nets"]
                    if cloudflare_enabled
                    else [],
                    sc.plugin_context["plugin.cloudflare"]["cloudflare_ipv6_nets"]
                    if cloudflare_enabled
                    else [],
                )
```

## Bottom line for your refactor

Changing each value in `fqdns.json` from a bare array to `{zone_id, origins}` is safe with zero code changes, because the program treats `fqdns.json` as a **set of FQDN keys** via a single `hostname not in proxied_fqdns` membership test (line 1652) and never touches the values. The only invariant you must preserve is that the top-level JSON stays an object keyed by FQDN string.</result>

## 1. Argument parser — `build_arg_parser()`

`/workspace/pantheon-sitehealth-emails`, lines **146–232**. Every boolean flag uses the identical idiom: `action="store_true"`, `default=False`, `help="..."`. The `dest` is implicit (derived from the long option, dashes → underscores, so `--for-real` → `sc.options.for_real`, `--only-warn` → `sc.options.only_warn`). `allow_abbrev=False` is set on the parser (line 150), so you must add both `--update-cloudflare-fqdns` and `--no-update-cloudflare-fqdns` explicitly rather than relying on prefix matching.

Verbatim excerpts of the relevant flags:

```python

## 3. Setup-hook system

Definitions in `/workspace/script_context.py`:

- `hooks` registry, lines **34–37**:
```python
34	hooks = {
35	    'setup': [],
36	    'check': [],
37	}
```
- `add_hook`, lines **53–57**:
```python
53	def add_hook(hook_name: str, target: dict) -&gt; None:
54	    if hook_name in hooks:
55	        hooks[hook_name].append(target)
56	    else:
57	        hooks[hook_name] = [target]
```
- `invoke_hooks`, lines **60–65**:
```python
60	def invoke_hooks(hook_name: str, *args, **kwargs) -&gt; None:
61	    debug(f'[bold magenta]=== Calling hooks for {hook_name}:')
62	    if hook_name in hooks:
63	        for hook in hooks[hook_name]:
64	            debug(f'Invoking {hook_name} hook target {hook["name"]}')
65	            hook['func'](*args, **kwargs)
```

**Hook dict shape:** `{'name': '&lt;dotted.path.identifier&gt;', 'func': &lt;callable&gt;}`. Hooks run in registration order; registration order = plugin load order (`find_modules("plugin")` walk in `main()`, line 1163). `invoke_hooks` forwards `*args, **kwargs` to each `func` — `setup` hooks are called with no extra args; `check` hooks are called with `site_context` (line 1561).

**Existing `setup` registrations:**
- `/workspace/plugin/cloudflare/__init__.py` line **13** (uses the raw list, not `add_hook`), gated on `[Cloudflare].enabled`:
```python
9	if 'Cloudflare' in sc.config and 'enabled' in sc.config['Cloudflare'] and sc.config['Cloudflare']['enabled']:
11	    from .ips import get_cloudflare_ips
12	    sc.plugin_context['plugin.cloudflare'] = {}
13	    sc.hooks['setup'].append({ 'name': 'plugin.cloudflare.ips.get_cloudflare_ips', 'func': get_cloudflare_ips})
```
- `/workspace/plugin/umich/__init__.py` line **7** (uses `add_hook`), gated on `[UMich].enabled`:
```python
5	if 'UMich' in sc.config and 'enabled' in sc.config['UMich'] and sc.config['UMich']['enabled']:
6	    from .portal import setup_portal_db, plan_info
7	    sc.add_hook('setup', {'name': 'plugin.umich.portal.setup_portal_db', 'func': setup_portal_db})
```
- `/workspace/plugin/aws/__init__.py` registers **no setup hook** — it registers a config `substitution` (lines 16–20), gated on `[AWS].enabled`. Shown as the other pattern for reference.

**Where setup hooks fire in `main()`** (`/workspace/pantheon-sitehealth-emails`): plugins are imported (which is when the `if enabled: ...append(...)` registration code above runs) at lines **1162–1166**; arg validation at 1177–1192; then:
```python
1198	    sc.invoke_hooks("setup")
1200	    sc.debug(f"Doing post-setup configuration substitutions")
1201	    sc.config = process_config(sc.config, deferred_pass=True)
```
This is **before** the per-site loop, which begins at line **1300** (`for site_name in sorted(site_name_to_id.keys()):`). So setup hooks run once, after config load / plugin import / arg validation / build-dir creation, and before any per-site work. (`check` hooks are invoked inside the loop at line **1561**.) The cloudflare setup hook `get_cloudflare_ips` populates `sc.plugin_context['plugin.cloudflare']['cloudflare_ipv4_nets'/'cloudflare_ipv6_nets']`, later read in the loop at lines ~1623–1626.

## 4. Progress bars / `rich` usage

There is **no** `rich.progress` / `Progress` / `track()` / `BarColumn` usage anywhere in the program, plugins, or checks. I searched `/workspace/pantheon-sitehealth-emails`, `/workspace/plugin`, and `/workspace/check`. The only progress-style UI is `rich` **spinners via `sc.console.status(...)`**:

- `/workspace/script_context.py` line **16**: `console = Console()` (this is `sc.console`).
- `/workspace/pantheon-sitehealth-emails` line **251**: `with sc.console.status(f"[bold green]Running: [bright_magenta]{commandline}"):` (wraps Terminus calls).
- `/workspace/plugin/cloudflare/ips.py` line **27**: `with sc.console.status('[bold green]Getting Cloudflare IP ranges ...'):`

`rich` imports in the main program are only `from rich.padding import Padding` (line 49) and `from rich.pretty import pprint` (line 50); plugins import `from rich.pretty import pprint`. Output elsewhere is `sc.console.print(...)` / `sc.debug(...)` (which calls `console.log`). So if you want a real progress bar for the Cloudflare-FQDN update across multiple sites, you'd be introducing `rich.progress` fresh — the established idiom in this codebase is the `sc.console.status(...)` spinner context manager, not a determinate bar.

## 5. `umich_enabled()` and `[Cloudflare]`/config gating

- `umich_enabled()` at `/workspace/pantheon-sitehealth-emails` lines **1137–1149** — the canonical gating pattern (also the model to copy for a `cloudflare_enabled()`-style helper):
```python
1145	    return (
1146	        "UMich" in sc.config
1147	        and "enabled" in sc.config["UMich"]
1148	        and sc.config["UMich"]["enabled"]
1149	    )
```
Call sites at lines **1307, 1930, 2275, 3716, 3747, 3829**.

- **Cloudflare enabled is detected two ways:**
  1. At plugin-import time in `/workspace/plugin/cloudflare/__init__.py` line **9**: `if 'Cloudflare' in sc.config and 'enabled' in sc.config['Cloudflare'] and sc.config['Cloudflare']['enabled']:` — only then is the plugin's `setup` hook registered and `sc.plugin_context['plugin.cloudflare']` created.
  2. In `main()` at `/workspace/pantheon-sitehealth-emails` line **1287**: `cloudflare_enabled = "plugin.cloudflare" in sc.plugin` — i.e. the runtime check is "did the cloudflare plugin get loaded" (which happens iff enabled). This `cloudflare_enabled` local is threaded into the per-site DNS logic (passed to the resolver at ~line 1622; nets read at ~1623–1626).

- **`[Cloudflare]` config values are read** in the setup hook `/workspace/plugin/cloudflare/ips.py` lines **15–25**: `cf = sc.config['Cloudflare']`, then `cf.get('api_token')`, else `cf.get('email')` + `cf.get('api_key')`.

- **Config gating mechanism** — `gate_disabled_sections()` at `/workspace/pantheon-sitehealth-emails` lines **843–858**, called in `main()` at line **1160** *before* substitution resolution. Any top-level section whose `enabled` is boolean `False` is reduced to `{'enabled': False}` (all other keys dropped), so a disabled section's `&lt;{secret ...}&gt;` values are never required. Sections without `enabled`, or with `enabled` truthy, are left intact.

### Practical notes for your feature
- Add the two flags in `build_arg_parser()` (~after line 199) following the `store_true`/`default=False`/`help` idiom; because `allow_abbrev=False`, define both `--update-cloudflare-fqdns` and `--no-update-cloudflare-fqdns` explicitly (or use `BooleanOptionalAction`). They will surface as `sc.options.update_cloudflare_fqdns` / `sc.options.no_update_cloudflare_fqdns`.
- "Processing multiple sites" = `sc.options.all or len(sc.options.sites) &gt; 1`, consistent with the validation at lines 1184–1187.
- Register any new FQDN-update work as a `setup` hook in `/workspace/plugin/cloudflare/__init__.py` (same gated `if` block, line 9), mirroring line 13; it will run at `sc.invoke_hooks("setup")` (line 1198), before the per-site loop (line 1300). Note the existing stale-`fqdns.json` + `--all` exit at lines 1570–1577, which your update feature likely supersedes.
- For any progress UI, the codebase precedent is `sc.console.status(...)` spinners (script_context line 16 `console`, main line 251, ips.py line 27); no determinate progress bar exists yet.</result>

1406	                f":exclamation: [bold red] ATTENTION: {site['name']} "
1407	                f"is on an unknown plan: {site['plan_name']}"
1408	            )
1409	            sys.exit("Bailing out.")
1410	
1411	        # From https://docs.pantheon.io/guides/account-mgmt/traffic/overages
1412	        # FAQ 1 as of April 25, 2024:
1413	        # "Only traffic for the Live environment is counted towards a site plan's traffic limit."
1414	
1415	        # The live environment will always exist, but may not be initialized.
1416	        envs, errors, fatal = terminus(
1417	            "env:list",
1418	            site["id"],
1419	            "--fields=id,created,domain,connection_mode,locked,initialized,php_version,php_runtime_generation",
1420	        )

1422	            # Transient/undecodable failure: skip this site, don't abort the whole run.
1423	            sc.console.print(
1424	                f":exclamation: [bold red] ERROR: could not fetch environments for {site_name}: {errors}"
1425	            )
1426	            continue

1428	            sc.console.print(
1429	                f":exclamation: [bold red] ERROR: {site['name']} does not have a live environment, "
1430	                "this should never happen"
1431	            )
1432	            sys.exit("Bailing out.")
1433	        if envs["live"]["initialized"] is False:
1434	            sc.console.print(
1435	                f":exclamation: [bold red] ERROR: {site['name']} is on a paid plan but its live "
1436	                "environment is not initialized"
1437	            )
1438	            site_context.add_notice(
1439	                {
1440	                    "type": "alert",
1441	                    "icon": "&#x1F6A8;",  # police car light
1442	                    "csv": f"{site['name']},no-live-env-but-paid-plan",
1443	                    "short": f"no live environment",
1444	                    "message": f"""
1445	            <p>{site["name"]} is on a paid plan but its live environment is not initialized.  Either initialize
1446	            the live environment and connect a domain through which people will access the site or downgrade the
1447	            site's plan to Sandbox to save money.</p>
1448	            """,
1449	                    "text": f"""
1450	            {site["name"]} is on a paid plan but its
1451	            live environment is not initialized.  Either initialize the
1452	            live environment and connect a domain through which people
1453	            will access the site or downgrade the site's plan to
1454	            Sandbox to save money.
1455	            """,
1456	                }
1457	            )

1466	            )

1471	        # in the loop below much faster.
1472	        _ = (
1473	            db_session.query(PantheonTraffic)
1474	            .filter(
1475	                PantheonTraffic.site_id == site["id"],
1476	                PantheonTraffic.traffic_date.between(start_date, end_date),
1477	            )
1478	            .all()
1479	        )
1480

1485	            ).date()

1487	                continue  # skip today's partial data

1494	                cache_hits=entry["cache_hits"],

1499	
1500	        if sc.options.import_older_metrics:
1501	            sc.console.print(
1502	                f"[bold magenta]=== Importing older metrics for {site['name']}:"
1503	            )
1504	
1505	            # Process old data by week:
1506	            new_rows = get_old_metrics(live_site, site, "week", end_date)
1507	            if len(new_rows) > 0:
1508	                if sc.config["Database"]["type"] == "sqlite":

1511	                            index_elements=["site_id", "traffic_date"]

1514	                    )
1515	                else:  # mysql:
1516	                    db_session.execute(
1517	                        insert(PantheonTraffic).prefix_with("IGNORE"), new_rows
1518	                    )
1519	                db_session.commit()
1520

1524	                if sc.config["Database"]["type"] == "sqlite":

1526	                        sqlite_insert(PantheonTraffic).on_conflict_do_nothing(
1527	                            index_elements=["site_id", "traffic_date"]
1528	                        ),
1529	                        new_rows,
1530	                    )
1531	                else:  # mysql:
1532	                    db_session.execute(
1533	                        insert(PantheonTraffic).prefix_with("IGNORE"), new_rows
1534	                    )
1535	                db_session.commit()
1536

1538

1556	            level=2,
1557	        )
1558	        # for row in results:
1559	        #    sc.debug(row, level=2)
1560	
1561	        sc.invoke_hooks("check", site_context)
1562	
1563	        # Get the list of all proxied Cloudflare FQDNs.
1564	        # This file is created by running the following cloudflare-support-tools command:
1565	        #   get_proxied_fqdns --output fqdns.json
1566	        # Warn if the file pointed to by the symlink is more than a day old.
1567	        proxied_fqdns_file = "fqdns.json"
1568	        if os.path.islink(proxied_fqdns_file):

1599	        not_in_dns = []
1600	        behind_cloudflare_not_proxied = []
1601	        if isinstance(domains, dict):
1602	            for d in domains.keys():

## Assistant

I now understand the consumption site fully. Critical structural facts:

- The `fqdns.json` read (lines 1563–1579) sits **inside the per-site loop** — it re-reads and re-stat's the file for every site, and it is **not** gated by `cloudflare_enabled`, so today the file is required even when Cloudflare is disabled (a latent bug). The actual *use* at line 1652 (`hostname not in proxied_fqdns`) **is** under `if cloudflare_enabled`.
- The old stale-file `--all` exit (1574–1577) is exactly what the new auto-update replaces.

This points to a clean design: a **second `setup` hook** in `plugin/cloudflare` that (when enabled) decides-whether-to-update, fetches+writes atomically, and loads the dict into `sc.plugin_context['plugin.cloudflare']['proxied_fqdns']`; the per-site loop then reads from plugin_context instead of re-opening the file. That also fixes the latent "file required when Cloudflare disabled" bug.

## Assistant

I now have a complete architectural picture. The design that fits the codebase cleanly:

- Add a **second `setup` hook** in `plugin/cloudflare/__init__.py` (gated on `[Cloudflare].enabled`) that decides-whether-to-update, fetches proxied FQDNs from the Cloudflare API (porting `get_proxied_fqdns`'s zones→proxied-DNS-records scan + rich progress bar), writes `fqdns.json` **atomically**, and loads the `{fqdn: {zone_id, origins}}` dict into `sc.plugin_context['plugin.cloudflare']['proxied_fqdns']`.
- Reuse the config-based client auth from `ips.py` (extract a shared `get_cloudflare_client()` helper — DRY).
- Replace the per-site file read (main script 1563–1579) with a read from plugin_context; the `hostname not in proxied_fqdns` check at 1652 is unchanged. This also fixes the latent bug where `fqdns.json` is required even when Cloudflare is disabled.
- Add `--update-cloudflare-fqdns` and `--no-update-cloudflare-fqdns` (mutually exclusive) to `build_arg_parser()`.

A few load-bearing decisions genuinely need your call before I finalize. Let me start with the core semantics.

## Assistant

Noted — you answered clearly:

1. **Account ID**: enumerate accounts via the `cloudflare` SDK (`accounts.list()`), scan zones per account — no hardcoded ID, no new config key. Most reusable.
2. **Fetch failure**: always fatal (named exception → abort).
3. **Write**: replace with a plain file via atomic temp + `os.replace` (drops the symlink convention; simplifies the mtime check since `getmtime` follows symlinks anyway).
4. **Traffic-only runs**: skip auto-update during `--update` / `--import-older-metrics`; `--only-warn` still updates.

Now the expansion opportunities — neutral posture, cherry-pick what you want. Rejected ones go to "NOT in scope."

### ⚙ Tool call: `Write`

```json
{
  "file_path": "/home/node/.claude/plans/development-2026-07-07-cloudflare-fqdns-luminous-kay.md",
  "content": "# Plan / Spec: Move `get_proxied_fqdns` into the program (Cloudflare plugin)\n\n> This document is the implementation spec. It was produced in plan mode, so it also\n> serves as the SPEC.md the PROMPT asks for: on approval, copy it to\n> `development/2026-07-07-cloudflare-fqdns/SPEC.md` (committed with the code) before/at\n> the start of implementation.\n\n## Context\n\nThe program currently reads a `fqdns.json` file (a map of every Cloudflare‑proxied website\nFQDN) that must be generated **out of band** by the standalone script\n`development/2026-07-07-cloudflare-fqdns/get_proxied_fqdns`. Operators have to remember to\nrun that script before a report run; if the file is stale and `--all` is used, the program\n**hard‑exits** telling them to regenerate it.\n\nThe goal is to fold that generation into the program's existing `cloudflare` plugin so the\ndata is fetched from the Cloudflare API on demand, and to enrich the file format with the\nCloudflare **zone ID** each FQDN came from (needed by a near‑future feature). The manual\nstep disappears; the file self‑refreshes under clear rules.\n\n### Verified facts (independently checked against the code, not just the prompt)\n\n- **`fqdns.json` is consumed in exactly one place** — `pantheon-sitehealth-emails:1652`,\n  `if hostname not in proxied_fqdns:`. Only the **dict keys** are used; values are never\n  read/indexed/iterated. → Changing values from `[origins]` to `{zone_id, origins}` breaks\n  **nothing**, and old array‑format files still load fine (keys unchanged).\n- The read block (`:1563–1579`) sits **inside the per‑site loop** and is **not** gated on\n  Cloudflare being enabled, so today the file is required on *every* run even when Cloudflare\n  is disabled — a latent bug this change removes. The *use* at `:1652` already sits under\n  `if cloudflare_enabled and not dns_transient:`.\n- The old stale‑file behavior (`:1570–1577`): warn always, and `sys.exit` if `--all`. The new\n  auto‑update replaces the exit.\n- Plugin/hook plumbing: `script_context.py` `hooks={'setup':[],'check':[]}`, `add_hook`,\n  `invoke_hooks`; setup hooks run once at `pantheon-sitehealth-emails:1198`\n  (`sc.invoke_hooks(\"setup\")`), **before** the per‑site loop (`:1300`). The cloudflare plugin\n  already registers one setup hook and a `sc.plugin_context['plugin.cloudflare']` bag\n  (`plugin/cloudflare/__init__.py:9–13`).\n- Arg parser (`build_arg_parser`, `:146–232`): `allow_abbrev=False`; boolean flags use\n  `action=\"store_true\", default=False`. Multi‑site detection = `sc.options.all or\n  len(sc.options.sites) > 1` (consistent with the validation at `:1184–1187`).\n- `--update` / `--import-older-metrics` `continue` at `:1537/1541`, **before** the fqdns\n  block → they never consume fqdns. `--only-warn` short‑circuits later (`:2928`) → it **does**\n  consume fqdns.\n- Cloudflare SDK `5.4.0` exposes `client.accounts.list()`, `client.zones.list(account=…)`,\n  `client.dns.records.list(zone_id=…, proxied=True)` (introspected). Zone objects have\n  `.id`/`.name`; records have `.name`/`.content`.\n- `fqdns.json` is **tracked in git *and*** listed in `.gitignore` (`/fqdns.json`). Writes will\n  show as modifications to the tracked file.\n\n### Decisions locked with the user\n\n| # | Decision | Choice |\n|---|----------|--------|\n| 1 | Cloudflare account source | **Enumerate accounts via the SDK** (`accounts.list()`), scan zones per account. **No hardcoded ID, no new config key.** |\n| 2 | Fetch failure | **Always fatal** — named exception, clear message, abort the run. No fallback. |\n| 3 | Write target | **Replace with a plain file** via atomic temp‑write + `os.replace` (drops the symlink/dated‑file convention). |\n| 4 | Traffic‑only runs | **Skip** auto‑update during `--update` and `--import-older-metrics`; `--only-warn` still updates. |\n| 5 | File path | **Hardcoded `\"fqdns.json\"`** (no config key). |\n| 6 | Staleness window | **Hardcoded 24 h** (86400 s). |\n| 7 | Concurrency | **Serial** zone scan (port as‑is). |\n| 8 | `no-certcheck` tag | **Include all proxied records** (do not port the filter). |\n\n### NOT in scope (explicitly deferred/rejected)\n\n- Configurable output path / staleness threshold (decisions 5–6).\n- Concurrent/threaded zone scanning (decision 7).\n- Porting `--no-certcheck` tag filtering (decision 8).\n- Touching the standalone `development/.../get_proxied_fqdns` (it stays as the archived\n  original; an external ITS inventory script still uses it — out of our repo's scope).\n- The `zone_id` value is **stored but not consumed** yet (future feature); no code reads it.\n- Untracking `fqdns.json` from git (`git rm --cached`) — noted as an optional operator cleanup,\n  not done here.\n\n---\n\n## Design\n\n### New/changed files\n\n```\nplugin/cloudflare/client.py   NEW  — get_cloudflare_client(): shared config-based auth\nplugin/cloudflare/ips.py      EDIT — use get_cloudflare_client() (DRY; remove inline auth)\nplugin/cloudflare/fqdns.py    NEW  — fetch/decide/write/load proxied FQDNs (the feature)\nplugin/cloudflare/__init__.py EDIT — register the second setup hook (when enabled)\npantheon-sitehealth-emails    EDIT — 2 new flags; remove per-site file read; read from\n                                     plugin_context; disabled+flag guard\n```\n\n### DRY: shared client factory (`client.py`)\n\n`ips.py` currently builds the `Cloudflare` client inline (`:15–25`). `fqdns.py` needs the\nsame auth. Extract it once:\n\n```python\n# plugin/cloudflare/client.py\nimport sys\nfrom cloudflare import Cloudflare\nimport script_context as sc\n\ndef get_cloudflare_client() -> Cloudflare:\n    \"\"\"Build a Cloudflare client from the [Cloudflare] config section.\n\n    api_token (preferred) else email + api_key.  No direct-environment fallback.\n    Exits with a clear message if credentials are missing while enabled.\n    \"\"\"\n    cf = sc.config['Cloudflare']\n    api_token = cf.get('api_token')\n    if api_token:\n        return Cloudflare(api_token=api_token)\n    email = cf.get('email')\n    api_key = cf.get('api_key')\n    if not email or not api_key:\n        sys.exit('ERROR: [Cloudflare] is enabled but needs either api_token, '\n                 'or both email and api_key.')\n    return Cloudflare(api_email=email, api_key=api_key)\n```\n\n`ips.py` becomes `client = get_cloudflare_client()` then `client.ips.list()`; the missing‑cred\n`sys.exit` and token/email selection move into the helper (behavior identical — existing\n`test_plugin_cloudflare.py` still passes because it fakes `sys.modules['cloudflare']` before\nload and monkeypatches `Cloudflare`; see Testing).\n\n### The feature (`fqdns.py`)\n\n```python\nFQDNS_FILE = \"fqdns.json\"\nSTALE_SECONDS = 24 * 60 * 60   # 86400\n\nclass CloudflareFqdnsError(Exception):\n    \"\"\"A Cloudflare API failure while fetching proxied FQDNs (always fatal).\"\"\"\n\ndef decide_fqdns_update(*, exists, age_seconds, multi_site, force, suppress, traffic_only):\n    \"\"\"Pure decision function → (should_update: bool, reason: str). No I/O.\"\"\"\n    if force:\n        return True, \"--update-cloudflare-fqdns requested\"\n    if traffic_only:\n        return False, \"traffic-only run (--update/--import-older-metrics); fqdns not consumed\"\n    if not exists:\n        return True, \"fqdns.json does not exist\"\n    if age_seconds > STALE_SECONDS and multi_site and not suppress:\n        return True, \"fqdns.json older than 24h and processing multiple sites\"\n    return False, \"fqdns.json present (fresh, single-site, or update suppressed)\"\n\ndef fetch_proxied_fqdns(client) -> dict:\n    \"\"\"accounts -> zones -> proxied DNS records -> {fqdn: {zone_id, origins:[...]}}.\n    Ports get_proxied_fqdns' progress bars (CFProgress + progress_bar).\n    Wraps cloudflare.CloudflareError -> CloudflareFqdnsError.\"\"\"\n\ndef write_fqdns_atomic(path, data):\n    \"\"\"tempfile.mkstemp in the target dir -> json.dump(indent=4, sort_keys=True) ->\n    os.replace(tmp, path).  Cleans up tmp on any exception (incl. KeyboardInterrupt).\n    Replacing onto a symlink path replaces the symlink with the plain file.\"\"\"\n\ndef update_and_load_proxied_fqdns():\n    \"\"\"setup-hook entry point (registered only when [Cloudflare].enabled).\"\"\"\n```\n\n**`update_and_load_proxied_fqdns()` orchestration:**\n\n```\nexists      = os.path.exists(FQDNS_FILE)\nage_seconds = (time.time() - os.path.getmtime(FQDNS_FILE)) if exists else None\nmulti_site  = sc.options.all or len(sc.options.sites) > 1\nforce       = sc.options.update_cloudflare_fqdns\nsuppress    = sc.options.no_update_cloudflare_fqdns\ntraffic_only= sc.options.update or sc.options.import_older_metrics\n\nshould, reason = decide_fqdns_update(exists=exists, age_seconds=age_seconds or 0,\n                                     multi_site=multi_site, force=force,\n                                     suppress=suppress, traffic_only=traffic_only)\nsc.debug(f\"Cloudflare fqdns update decision: {should} ({reason})\")\n\nif should:\n    sc.console.print(f\"[bold green]Updating {FQDNS_FILE} from Cloudflare ({reason}) ...\")\n    client = get_cloudflare_client()\n    data = fetch_proxied_fqdns(client)     # may raise CloudflareFqdnsError -> caught -> sys.exit\n    write_fqdns_atomic(FQDNS_FILE, data)\n    sc.console.print(f\"[bold green]Wrote {len(data)} proxied FQDNs to {FQDNS_FILE}.\")\n    proxied = data\nelse:\n    if exists and age_seconds > STALE_SECONDS:\n        sc.console.print(f\":exclamation: [bold red] ATTENTION: {FQDNS_FILE} is more than a day old!\")\n    proxied = _load_existing(FQDNS_FILE)   # {} if missing (only reachable in traffic-only)\n\nsc.plugin_context[\"plugin.cloudflare\"][\"proxied_fqdns\"] = proxied\n```\n\n`CloudflareFqdnsError` is caught here → `sc.console.print` the error → `sys.exit(...)` (decision\n2: always fatal). `_load_existing` tolerates old array‑format and new object‑format (keys only).\n\n### Registration (`__init__.py`, inside the existing `if …enabled:` block)\n\n```python\nfrom .fqdns import update_and_load_proxied_fqdns\nsc.hooks['setup'].append({'name': 'plugin.cloudflare.fqdns.update_and_load_proxied_fqdns',\n                          'func': update_and_load_proxied_fqdns})\n```\n\n### Main‑script edits (`pantheon-sitehealth-emails`)\n\n1. **`build_arg_parser()`** — add a mutually‑exclusive group (so contradiction is an argparse\n   error, a *named* failure):\n   ```python\n   cf_group = args_parser.add_mutually_exclusive_group()\n   cf_group.add_argument(\"--update-cloudflare-fqdns\", action=\"store_true\", default=False,\n       help=\"force-refresh fqdns.json from Cloudflare before this run (requires [Cloudflare] enabled)\")\n   cf_group.add_argument(\"--no-update-cloudflare-fqdns\", action=\"store_true\", default=False,\n       help=\"suppress the automatic stale-file refresh of fqdns.json\")\n   ```\n   → `sc.options.update_cloudflare_fqdns` / `sc.options.no_update_cloudflare_fqdns`.\n\n2. **Disabled‑plugin guard** (after `find_modules`/validation, ~`:1177–1192`, before\n   `invoke_hooks`):\n   ```python\n   if sc.options.update_cloudflare_fqdns and \"plugin.cloudflare\" not in sc.plugin:\n       sys.exit(\"--update-cloudflare-fqdns requires the [Cloudflare] section to be enabled in the config.\")\n   ```\n   (`--no-update-…` on a disabled plugin is a harmless no‑op.)\n\n3. **Remove the per‑site file read** (delete `:1563–1579`) and change the consumption at\n   `:1652` to read from plugin context:\n   ```python\n   if hostname not in sc.plugin_context[\"plugin.cloudflare\"][\"proxied_fqdns\"]:\n   ```\n   This line already runs only under `if cloudflare_enabled and not dns_transient:`, so the\n   `plugin.cloudflare` bag and its `proxied_fqdns` key always exist there.\n\n### Diagrams\n\n**Update‑decision flow (in `decide_fqdns_update`)**\n\n```\n                      ┌───────────────────────────┐\n   --update-cloudflare-fqdns? ─yes─────────────────┼──► UPDATE (\"forced\")\n                      │no                          │\n   --update / --import-older-metrics? ─yes─────────┼──► SKIP  (\"traffic-only\")\n                      │no                          │\n   fqdns.json missing? ─yes────────────────────────┼──► UPDATE (\"missing\")\n                      │no                          │\n   age>24h AND multi-site AND not --no-update? ─yes─┼──► UPDATE (\"stale+multi\")\n                      │no                          │\n                      └────────────────────────────┴──► SKIP  (use existing; warn if stale)\n```\n\n**Data flow (setup hook, runs once before the per‑site loop)**\n\n```\n[Cloudflare] enabled\n   │  sc.invoke_hooks(\"setup\")  (pantheon-sitehealth-emails:1198)\n   ▼\nget_cloudflare_client() ──► Cloudflare API\n   │                          accounts.list() ─► for each account:\n   │                            zones.list(account) ─► for each zone (progress bar):\n   │                              dns.records.list(zone_id, proxied=True)\n   ▼\n{fqdn: {zone_id, origins:[content,…]}}\n   │  write_fqdns_atomic(tmp → os.replace → fqdns.json)   (plain file)\n   ▼\nsc.plugin_context[\"plugin.cloudflare\"][\"proxied_fqdns\"]\n   │\n   ▼  per-site loop (:1652)  — key membership test only\n`hostname not in proxied_fqdns`  ─► behind_cloudflare_not_proxied / fqdns_behind_cloudflare\n```\n\n### Shadow paths & edge cases (Prime Directives 1–4)\n\n- **Empty result** (0 accounts or 0 zones or 0 proxied records): writes `{}` and prints a\n  loud warning `ATTENTION: Cloudflare returned N accounts / M zones / 0 proxied FQDNs`. Not\n  fatal (could be a legitimately tiny org), but visible — otherwise every custom domain would\n  silently flag \"not proxied.\"\n- **API error** (auth/network/rate‑limit) → `CloudflareFqdnsError` → caught → `sys.exit`\n  (fatal). Catch the SDK base `cloudflare.CloudflareError` **specifically**, not bare\n  `Exception` (verify the exact class at implementation; 5.4.0 base is `CloudflareError`).\n- **Missing credentials while enabled** → `get_cloudflare_client()` `sys.exit` (existing\n  behavior, now shared).\n- **User interrupts (Ctrl‑C) mid‑fetch/write** → temp file cleaned up in `write_fqdns_atomic`'s\n  `except`; existing `fqdns.json` untouched; `KeyboardInterrupt` propagates and the run exits.\n- **Same FQDN in ≥2 zones / ≥2 records**: append `content` to `origins`; **keep the first\n  zone_id**; if a *different* zone_id is seen for the same FQDN, `sc.console.print` a warning\n  (visible, first‑zone‑wins is deterministic).\n- **Old array‑format file on disk**: `_load_existing` loads it; only keys are used, so it\n  works until the next update rewrites it in the new format.\n- **`fqdns.json` symlink present on first run**: `os.path.getmtime` follows it for the age\n  check; `os.replace` replaces the symlink itself with the new plain file (decision 3).\n- **Disabled Cloudflare**: hook never registers; nothing fetched/read; consumption skipped.\n  Fixes the old \"file required even when disabled\" bug.\n\n---\n\n## Testing (extends the existing harness — no parallel approach)\n\nFollow `tests/integration/test_plugin_cloudflare.py`'s pattern: fake `cloudflare` in\n`sys.modules` before loading the module via `SourceFileLoader`, monkeypatch `Cloudflare`,\nset `sc.config`/`sc.plugin_context` by hand, use `tmp_path` as cwd for file writes. Reuse\n`psh`, `reset_sc`, `monkeypatch`. Never run the program except via `run_program`; never use\n`--all`/`--for-real`/live `--create-tables`.\n\n### Unit — `tests/unit/test_fqdns_decision.py` (`pytest.mark.unit`)\n- Load `plugin/cloudflare/fqdns.py` (fake `cloudflare` module first, like the sibling).\n- **Table test** of `decide_fqdns_update` covering every branch: force→update; traffic_only\n  (no force)→skip; force beats traffic_only; missing (non‑traffic)→update; stale+multi+not‑suppress\n  →update; stale+multi+suppress→skip; stale+single→skip; fresh+multi→skip.\n- **Hypothesis property**: `force ⇒ update`; `traffic_only ∧ ¬force ⇒ ¬update`; result is always\n  a `(bool, str)` with a non‑empty reason. (Pure function, no I/O — good fuzz target.)\n\n### Integration — `tests/integration/test_plugin_cloudflare_fqdns.py` (`pytest.mark.integration`)\nFake SDK exposing `accounts.list()`, `zones.list(account=…)`, `dns.records.list(zone_id=…,\nproxied=…)` returning `SimpleNamespace`/lists with `.id`/`.name`/`.content`.\n- **`fetch_proxied_fqdns`** builds `{fqdn: {zone_id, origins}}` correctly: single record;\n  multiple records for one FQDN merge origins; **same FQDN across two zones** keeps the first\n  `zone_id` and emits the conflict warning; multiple accounts are all scanned.\n- **`write_fqdns_atomic`** into `tmp_path`: writes valid JSON (indent/sort), and when the target\n  is a pre‑existing **symlink**, the result is a **plain file** (not a symlink) with the data.\n- **`update_and_load_proxied_fqdns`** in‑process, cwd=`tmp_path`, `sc.config['Cloudflare']`\n  enabled, `sc.plugin_context={'plugin.cloudflare':{}}`, `sc.options` via `psh.parse_args([...])`:\n  - `--update-cloudflare-fqdns` → writes file + populates `plugin_context['plugin.cloudflare']['proxied_fqdns']`.\n  - missing file (report run) → fetches; **fresh single‑site** existing file → no fetch (assert the\n    fake client's list methods were **not** called), loads existing.\n  - **fetch raises** `cloudflare.CloudflareError` → `SystemExit` (fatal).\n  - old array‑format existing file + no‑update path → loads, keys usable.\n- **Client factory** auth‑selection tests (`api_token` preferred; `email`+`api_key`; missing →\n  `SystemExit`): either keep them where they are in `test_plugin_cloudflare.py` (they still\n  pass — the logic just moved to `client.py`, imported by `ips.py`) or move them alongside\n  `client.py`. Keeping them is the smaller diff; verify green either way.\n\n### e2e / golden — no new golden; assert non‑regression\n- All offline e2e configs have `[Cloudflare] enabled = false` (`minimal.toml`,\n  `minimal-nonumich.toml`) → the new hook never registers, the removed per‑site read changes\n  nothing observable → **goldens must stay byte‑identical without `--update-goldens`.**\n  Verify: `grep -n 'enabled' tests/fixtures/config/minimal*.toml` shows Cloudflare false; run\n  `./run-tests --fast` and confirm goldens pass unchanged.\n- **Keep** `make_workdir`'s fresh `fqdns.json = \"{}\"` stub (`conftest.py:154–167`) — update its\n  comment. It now doubles as an **offline guard**: if any subprocess run ever uses a\n  Cloudflare‑enabled config, a fresh empty file makes `decide_fqdns_update` return \"skip\" (exists\n  + fresh + single‑site), so **no real API call** happens in a subprocess (which can't inject a\n  fake SDK). Confirm no `run_program(...)` call uses a Cloudflare‑enabled config:\n  `grep -rn 'full.toml' tests/` should show only in‑process loads, not `run_program`.\n\n### Acceptance criteria (exact commands → observable outcomes)\n1. `./run-tests --fast` → **green**, goldens unchanged (no `--update-goldens` needed).\n2. `./run-tests -m \"unit or integration\" -k fqdns` → new tests **green**.\n3. `./run-tests` (full, incl. `live`) → **green**.\n4. `./pantheon-sitehealth-emails --update-cloudflare-fqdns --no-update-cloudflare-fqdns …`\n   → argparse error \"not allowed with argument\".\n5. ### ↳ Tool result

```
I've verified the spec's key claims against the codebase. Here is my review.

---

# Independent Review: `development-2026-07-07-cloudflare-fqdns-luminous-kay.md`

## 1. Completeness — **ISSUES**

**1.1 (High) The disabled-plugin guard checks the wrong condition and becomes a silent no-op.**
The spec (lines 214-217, acceptance criterion #5) guards with:
```python
if sc.options.update_cloudflare_fqdns and "plugin.cloudflare" not in sc.plugin:
    sys.exit(...)
```
But `find_modules("plugin")` (verified at `pantheon-sitehealth-emails:861-874`) walks for any **non-empty `__init__.py`** and returns `plugin.cloudflare` **regardless of `[Cloudflare].enabled`**; `main()` then unconditionally does `sc.plugin[plugin_name] = module` (`:1166`). The enabled-gating lives *inside* `__init__.py` (whether to register the hook), not in whether the package is imported. So `"plugin.cloudflare"` is **always** in `sc.plugin`, the guard **never fires**, and `--update-cloudflare-fqdns` against a disabled config sails past the guard, then the fqdns hook was never registered → **the flag silently does nothing**. This directly violates Prime Directive 1 (no silent failures) and **fails acceptance criterion #5** as written.
*Fix:* gate on config, e.g. `if sc.options.update_cloudflare_fqdns and not sc.config.get('Cloudflare', {}).get('enabled'):`.

**1.2 (Low) `_load_existing` is referenced but never defined.** Used at lines 183/189 and central to the "old array-format still loads" guarantee, but its behavior (format tolerance, missing-file → `{}`, malformed-JSON handling) is never specified. A competent implementer must invent it.

**1.3 (Low) Empty-result warning promises counts the fetch function doesn't produce.** The shadow-path text (line 269) prints `ATTENTION: Cloudflare returned N accounts / M zones / 0 proxied FQDNs`, but the `fetch_proxied_fqdns` contract (lines 144-147) returns only the `{fqdn: …}` dict — it never specifies returning/emitting account/zone counts. Under-specified.

**1.4 (Medium, judgment call) Writing `{}` on an authz-scoped token is a quiet trap.** If a token authenticates but lacks DNS:Read on some/all zones, `fetch` returns `{}`, `write` persists it, and the *next* consumption flags **every** custom domain "not proxied." The only mitigation is one console line that will scroll past in a long `--all` run. Given decision 2 ("fetch failure = always fatal"), consider treating "authenticated but 0 zones/records" as loud-and-fatal rather than a silent successful `{}` write.

## 2. Consistency — **ISSUES**

**2.1 (High) The client.py claim contradicts how the existing test actually works.** See 5.1 — the spec asserts (lines 120-121, 322-324) the existing tests "still pass"; they do not.

**2.2 (Low) Decision 2 says "named exception," but missing-creds uses bare `sys.exit`.** `get_cloudflare_client` exits with a string (line 113), not `CloudflareFqdnsError`. The spec acknowledges these are different failure modes, so this is minor, but it's a slight tension with the "named errors" directive.

**Verified-consistent (PASS):** the `:1652` consumption is indeed key-membership only (confirmed at `pantheon-sitehealth-emails:1652`), so array→`{zone_id, origins}` breaks nothing; the use already sits under `if cloudflare_enabled and not dns_transient:` (`:1645`); `--update`/`--import` `continue` at `:1537/1541` before the fqdns block (confirmed); arg-parser conventions match.

## 3. Clarity — **MOSTLY PASS**

Generally implementable. Gaps: `_load_existing` (1.2), the empty-result count wording (1.3), and the same-FQDN-across-zones "warning" (line 280) doesn't say via what channel/format — implementable but left to the reader.

## 4. Scope — **PASS**

Disciplined. The eight decisions and the "NOT in scope" list are honored in the design. The `client.py` extraction is a small, justified DRY refactor rather than creep. `zone_id` is stored-but-unused per plan, correctly flagged.

## 5. Feasibility — **ISSUES**

**5.1 (High, CONFIRMED) Moving auth into `client.py` breaks `test_plugin_cloudflare.py`, contrary to the spec's explicit claim.** Two independent reasons:
- **Broken monkeypatch seam.** All five tests rely on `monkeypatch.setattr(module, "Cloudflare", …)` where `module` is the standalone-loaded **ips.py** (`test_plugin_cloudflare.py:44,60,73,84,95,105`). After the refactor, `get_cloudflare_ips` calls `get_cloudflare_client()`, and the `Cloudflare` name is bound in **client.py's** globals — the ips.py monkeypatch no longer intercepts client construction. The fake `cloudflare` module only supplies `Cloudflare = object` as a **placeholder** (line 44), so the three auth-assertion tests (`test_auth_prefers_api_token`, `test_auth_uses_email_and_api_key`, `test_auth_missing_credentials_exits`) and `test_client_failure_exits` / `test_cidrs_become_ip_networks` would hit `object(api_email=…)` → `TypeError`, not the fake. **These tests fail.**
- **Standalone relative-import failure.** The fixture loads `ips.py` via `SourceFileLoader("cloudflare_ips_probe", …)` with **no package context**. `ips.py` currently has *no* relative imports (verified — only `from cloudflare import …`, `import script_context`), which is *why* the standalone load works. Adding `from .client import get_cloudflare_client` raises `ImportError: attempted relative import with no known parent package` at `exec_module` time, erroring the fixture and **all five tests**.

The spec's line 121 ("existing `test_plugin_cloudflare.py` still passes") and lines 322-324 ("they still pass … Keeping them is the smaller diff") are **incorrect**. The tests must be reworked to import the plugin files as real package modules (so relative imports resolve) and monkeypatch `Cloudflare`/`get_cloudflare_client` in the right namespace.

**5.2 (High, same root cause) The specified `fqdns.py` integration tests won't load either.** The plan says load `fqdns.py` "like the sibling" (standalone `SourceFileLoader`, line 299), but `fqdns.py` calls `get_cloudflare_client()` (line 175), presumably via `from .client import …` — the same standalone relative-import failure. The whole "fake `cloudflare` in `sys.modules` + `SourceFileLoader`" pattern is incompatible with any plugin file that imports a sibling plugin file. The testing approach needs a package-aware loader, which the spec does not describe.

**Verified-feasible (PASS):** the "changing values doesn't break consumption" claim (5.1 of the prompt's ask) is correct — `:1652` is pure key membership. The SDK surface (`zones.list(account=…)`, `dns.records.list(zone_id=…, proxied=True)`) matches the working standalone `get_proxied_fqdns` (`:116,127`); `accounts.list()` is plausible but the only call **not** exercised by the existing standalone — worth a 1-line runtime check at implementation, low risk.

---

## Overall: **6 / 10**

**Verdict:** Thorough, well-reasoned design with correct core claims (consumption/format safety, hook timing), but two confirmed landmines — the disabled-plugin guard is a silent no-op that fails its own acceptance criterion #5, and the "existing Cloudflare tests still pass after the client.py extraction" claim is false on two counts — both must be fixed before implementation.

861:def find_modules(module_type: str) -> list[str]:
    return data


def gate_disabled_sections(config: dict) -> dict:
    """For every top-level section whose `enabled` is the boolean False, keep only
    {'enabled': False} and drop the section's other settings.

    Done BEFORE substitution resolution (process_config) so a disabled feature never forces its
    `<{secret env ...}>` / `<{secret aws ...}>` values to exist -- turning a feature off must not
    require its credentials to be present.  Sections without an `enabled` key, or whose `enabled`
    is anything other than the boolean False (e.g. True, or the string "false"), are left
    untouched.  Only top-level tables are considered; nested tables like [Pantheon.plan_info]
    are unaffected.
    """
    for name, value in list(config.items()):
        if isinstance(value, dict) and value.get("enabled") is False:
            sc.debug(f"Section [{name}] is disabled; keeping only 'enabled', dropping other keys")
            config[name] = {"enabled": False}
    return config


def find_modules(module_type: str) -> list[str]:
    modules = []
    # find all non-empty regular files in/under the directory f"{type}" that are named "__init__.py":
    for dirpath, dirs, files in os.walk(module_type, followlinks=True):
        for file in files:
            if file == "__init__.py":
                target = os.path.join(dirpath, file)
                st = os.stat(target)
                if stat.S_ISREG(st.st_mode) and st.st_size != 0:
                    parts = target.split("/")[:-1]
                    target_name = ".".join(parts)
                    modules.append(target_name)
    modules.sort()  # ensure a consistent order when importing to simplify troubleshooting
    return modules


def smtp_login() -> SMTP_SSL:
    smtp_cfg = sc.config.get("SMTP", {})
    host = smtp_cfg.get("host", "smtp.mail.umich.edu")
    port = smtp_cfg.get("port", 465)

    with open(sc.options.config, "rb") as f:
        sc.config = tomllib.load(f)

    # Drop the non-`enabled` settings of any disabled section BEFORE substitution resolution,
    # so a disabled feature's <{secret env ...}> values are never required to exist.
    sc.config = gate_disabled_sections(sc.config)

    sc.debug(f"[bold magenta]=== Loading plugins:")
    for plugin_name in find_modules("plugin"):
        sc.debug(f"Loading plugin: {plugin_name}")
        module = importlib.import_module(plugin_name)
        sc.plugin[plugin_name] = module

    sc.debug(f"Doing pre-setup configuration substitutions")
    sc.config = process_config(sc.config)

    sc.debug(f"[bold magenta]=== Loading checks:")
    for check_name in find_modules("check"):
        sc.debug(f"Loading check: {check_name}")
        module = importlib.import_module(check_name)
        sc.check[check_name] = module

    # Validate and process arguments
    if sc.options.create_tables:
        if sc.options.import_older_metrics:
            sys.exit(
                "The --import-older-metrics and --create-tables options are mutually exclusive."
            )
        sc.options.verbose = 3  # force verbose output
    elif (sc.options.all and len(sc.options.sites) != 0) or (
        not sc.options.all and len(sc.options.sites) == 0
    ):
        sys.exit("You must specify either at least one site or the --all option.")

        pprint(sc.options)
        self_info, _errors, _fatal = terminus("self:info")
        pprint(self_info)

- So the existing `cloudflare_enabled = "plugin.cloudflare" in sc.plugin` (line 1287) is a **pre-existing latent bug** — always True — that would `KeyError` on `sc.plugin_context["plugin.cloudflare"]["cloudflare_ipv4_nets"]` for a disabled adopter with custom domains (masked today only because U-M always enables Cloudflare and the offline e2e uses platform-only domains).

A cross‑file **relative** import\n(`from .client import …`) raises `ImportError: attempted relative import with no known parent\npackage` under that loader, and the monkeypatch would target the wrong namespace — breaking all\nfive existing cloudflare tests. Reworking the harness to be package‑aware is a bigger change than\nthis feature warrants. So `fqdns.py` carries its **own** inline client builder, mirroring\n`ips.py`, with a comment noting the intentional mirror (consolidate only if the harness later\nbecomes package‑aware). Net cost: ~8 duplicated lines; net benefit: zero churn to existing\ntested code, each plugin file stays standalone‑loadable.\n\n```python\n# in fqdns.py — mirrors get_cloudflare_ips' auth (kept inline so this file stays\n# standalone-loadable by tests/integration/test_plugin_cloudflare*.py)\ndef _cloudflare_client():\n    cf = sc.config['Cloudflare']\n    api_token = cf.get('api_token')\n    if api_token:\n        return Cloudflare(api_token=api_token)\n    email = cf.get('email'); api_key = cf.get('api_key')\n    if not email or not api_key:\n        sys.exit('ERROR: [Cloudflare] is enabled but needs either api_token, '\n                 'or both email and api_key.')\n    return Cloudflare(api_email=email, api_key=api_key)\n```"

# Round-2 Review: Cloudflare FQDNs Spec

## Verification of the two HIGH fixes

**Fix (A) — `cloudflare_enabled` detection + disabled-plugin guard: CORRECT.**

Confirmed against the code:
- `find_modules("plugin")` (script ~1163) imports *every* non-empty `__init__.py` package unconditionally, so `"plugin.cloudflare" in sc.plugin` at `:1287` is indeed always-True — the latent bug is real, and the replacement `bool(sc.config.get("Cloudflare", {}).get("enabled"))` fixes it.
- `gate_disabled_sections` (`:843–858`) reduces a `[Cloudflare]` with boolean `enabled = false` to `{'enabled': False}` *before* plugin load (`:1160`), so `.get("enabled")` returns `False` → `bool(...)` = `False`. Correct for the disabled case.
- Section **entirely absent**: `.get("Cloudflare", {})` → `{}` → `.get("enabled")` → `None` → guard's `not None` = True → clean exit "requires [Cloudflare] section to be enabled." Correct.
- Enabled case: `enabled` boolean `True` is left untouched by the gate → `bool(True)` = True; both old and new expressions agree. Enabled behavior unchanged.
- The guard fires correctly when disabled/absent because it reads `sc.config` *after* gating. Placement (after validation, before `invoke_hooks`) is sound.

**Golden non-regression holds.** The custom-domain loop (`:1601–1658`) skips `type == "platform"` domains (`:1604`), and the offline `domain:list` fixture is platform-only, so `classify_hostname_dns` and every `cloudflare_enabled`-gated line never execute in the goldens. The only other use, the `sc.debug` line at `:1288`, is console output not captured in the HTML/txt/eml goldens. Grep confirms **no test** asserts on the "Cloudflare is enabled/DISABLED" string or the old `in sc.plugin` expression. Flipping `cloudflare_enabled` True→False in the offline runs is therefore unobservable. Claim verified.

**Fix (B) — inline client, no `client.py`: CORRECT and sound.** `ips.py` is genuinely untouched, so `test_plugin_cloudflare.py` (which monkeypatches `module.Cloudflare` after a standalone `SourceFileLoader` load) stays green. A new `fqdns.py` with its own top-level `from cloudflare import Cloudflare` + inline `_cloudflare_client()` is loadable and monkeypatchable by the identical pattern. The relative-import hazard is correctly avoided. The ~8 duplicated lines are a reasonable trade against reworking the loader.

---

## Five dimensions

### Completeness
Issues:
1. **The test spec omits that the fake `cloudflare` module must define a real `CloudflareError` exception class.** `fetch_proxied_fqdns` catches `cloudflare.CloudflareError` and the "fetch raises → SystemExit" integration test depends on it, but §Integration only lists `accounts.list()/zones.list()/dns.records.list()` on the fake. Under the standalone loader the fake module is the one that resolves `cloudflare.CloudflareError`. *Fix:* have the fake set `fake_pkg.CloudflareError = type("CloudflareError", (Exception,), {})`, and note that `fqdns.py` needs **both** `import cloudflare` (for the `except`) and `from cloudflare import Cloudflare`.

### Consistency
Issues:
1. **Zero-zones raise vs. the `CloudflareError→CloudflareFqdnsError` wrap could self-swallow.** `fetch_proxied_fqdns` both "wraps `cloudflare.CloudflareError`" and "raises `CloudflareFqdnsError` on zero zones." If the deliberate zero-zone `raise CloudflareFqdnsError` sits inside the same `try` that converts `CloudflareError`, it's fine (different type), but this must be implemented so the zero-zone check runs *after* the API-iteration `try` block, not nested where a broad except could reinterpret it. Worth an explicit implementation note; not a spec defect per se.

Otherwise consistent: `multi_site = all or len(sites) > 1` matches the validation-site logic; `traffic_only` correctly mirrors that `--update`/`--import-older-metrics` never consume fqdns; the removed local `proxied_fqdns` (`:1579`) has exactly one remaining reader (`:1652`), now redirected to plugin context — no dangling reference.

### Clarity
PASS. The decision table, orchestration pseudocode, and shadow-path list are precise. The `age_seconds` None-safety is fine: the `else`-branch warning `if exists and age_seconds > STALE_SECONDS` short-circuits on `exists=False` before any `None > int` comparison.

### Scope
Issues:
1. **Zero-zones = always-fatal (decision 2) will hard-block a legitimately empty-but-enabled Cloudflare account with no override.** This is a locked decision, but the spec should state the consequence plainly: an adopter whose token authenticates against an account that genuinely has zero zones cannot run the tool at all. Given the reasoning (empty ⇒ likely DNS:Read scope problem) this is defensible, but call it out in the operator doc.
2. **`--create-tables` + `--update-cloudflare-fqdns` (enabled) is unspecified.** Setup hooks run at `:1198` before `--create-tables` exits at `:1235`, so the fqdns fetch/write would happen during a schema-creation run. Harmless (the user asked to force-refresh), but undocumented. Optional: note it or short-circuit.

### Feasibility
PASS. Every cited line/offset matches the real file (arg parser, `:1163–1166`, `:1177–1198`, `:1287`, `:1563–1579`, `:1652`, `gate_disabled_sections`). The hook/plugin_context plumbing exists as described (`__init__.py:12` sets the bag; the new hook always sets `proxied_fqdns`). The offline-guard reasoning around the conftest stub is workable — grep confirms no `run_program` call uses a Cloudflare-enabled config.

Minor feasibility nit:
1. **The conftest `fqdns.json = "{}"` stub is now largely vestigial**, not a live guard. With the disabled offline configs, the per-site read is gone *and* the hook never registers, so the stub is never read. Its "prevents a live API call in a subprocess" value only materializes for a hypothetical enabled subprocess config that does not exist in the suite. The comment update should say this honestly rather than framing it as an active safeguard.

---

## Adversarial review result

Your doc survived **2 rounds** of independent adversarial review. **2 HIGH issues + several minor** caught and fixed. Final quality score: **8/10** (round-2 minors now also addressed).

- **Round 1 (6/10)** caught two real landmines:
  1. The disabled-plugin guard `"plugin.cloudflare" not in sc.plugin` would **never fire** — every plugin package is imported regardless of `enabled` — and, worse, the *existing* `cloudflare_enabled = "plugin.cloudflare" in sc.plugin` (line 1287) is **always True**, a latent bug that would `KeyError` for a Cloudflare-disabled adopter with custom domains. I verified this empirically. → Fixed by reading config (`bool(sc.config.get("Cloudflare", {}).get("enabled"))`), which also fixes the pre-existing bug.
  2. Extracting a shared `client.py` would **break all five existing Cloudflare tests** (relative-import failure under the standalone `SourceFileLoader` + wrong monkeypatch namespace). → Dropped the extraction; `fqdns.py` carries a small intentional inline auth mirror, `ips.py` untouched.
- **Round 2 (8/10)** confirmed both fixes correct against the code and flagged only doc/test-fixture polish (fake `CloudflareError` class, zero-zones raise placement, operator-doc call-outs), all now applied.

## What the plan does

Move `get_proxied_fqdns` into the `cloudflare` plugin as a **second `setup` hook** that (when `[Cloudflare]` is enabled) decides whether to refresh, fetches proxied FQDNs (accounts → zones → proxied DNS records) with a progress bar, writes `fqdns.json` **atomically** in the new `{zone_id, origins}` shape, and loads it into `sc.plugin_context`. The one consumer (`hostname not in proxied_fqdns`, keys-only) reads from plugin_context instead of re-opening the file per site. Two new flags `--update-cloudflare-fqdns` / `--no-update-cloudflare-fqdns` (mutually exclusive). Locked to your 8 decisions; tests extend the existing harness; goldens stay byte-identical.

Full spec (with decision table, diagrams, shadow-path analysis, test plan, acceptance criteria, and doc updates) is in the plan file. On approval I'll copy it to `development/2026-07-07-cloudflare-fqdns/SPEC.md` and implement in order: `fqdns.py` → `__init__.py` → main-script edits → tests → docs → `./run-tests`.
